I visited here with my friend as we were looking to satisfy our vegan palates as well as enjoy some good Abyssinian/Ethiopian food. This place had come with good recommendations, so we were excited to give it a try. However, upon entering, at about 8pm on a Friday, we were informed that they had run out of food. As a small restaurant, I can understand the need to limit waste, but for a Friday night, one would think they'd have planned ahead. < Review>
I don't get it. I came here because I was in the area, was wanting mexican, and the reviews were great. Did I get the off night? The food was not good and it was not a good value for what I got. I ordered a fish taco / enchilada combo and carne asada combo. I was looking forward to it too. The fish tacos are literally frozen fish sticks in a corn tortilla. I couldn't believe it. It was placed directly on the cheese enchilada in my combo which made the taco fall apart. The enchilada was just ok. The carne asada was basically burnt ground beef. Definitely not the asada I've had many many times in the past. The rice and beans was bland and under seasoned too. To top if all off there is an unannounced 4% service charge added. (I was a walk in customer...not delivery) so when I got the receipt after I paid, I saw that I paid an extra 4% on top of my gratuity bringing my total bill to nearly $40 for this meal. Sorry, that's not a good value at all...especially for what I got.<//Review>

<Text>A preferred spot for delicious Mexican food. Do yourself a favor and give this place a try. I look forward to a return visit. The bill was decent for the quality.<//Text><pictures>None<//pictures><resp>None</resp><GmapID>0x80dcdf9f8f72c4ef:0xa7056f656417f82b</GmapID></record>

<Gmap_id>0x80dcdf9f8f72c4ef:0xa7056f656417f82b< /Gmap_id>< Response>
None<//Response>
< Review>
Perhaps to better describe its excellent carne deshebrada to Orange County, "Roman's Mexican Restaurant and Taqueria" has followed Chipotle in naming it "beef barbacoa," even though barbacoa in Spanish translates to barbecue and, in Mexico, barbacoa traditionally refers to pit-roasted meats.

I am 100% sure the owner of Roman's is aware that carne deshebrada, aka Mexican-style shredded beef, is not barbacoa. Carne deshebrada is culinarily closer to being the Mexican equivalent to the Caribbean-style marinated, slow-cooked beef referred to as "ropa vieja."

Roman's "Carne Deshebrada Taco" aka "Barbacoa Taco," consists of two thin white corn tortillas filled with braised beef, dressed with fresh chopped onions and cilantro. Roman's juicy carne deshebrada, due to lengthy stewing in chilies and spices, really doesn't require any additional sauce. Nonetheless, I added the salsa bar's thick salsa roja during my visit, and the smoldering combination induced delirium. This is not barbacoa, it's not even just carne deshebrada, it's heaven in a tortilla.< /Review>

< Text>
The best round of golf I have played so far in the Reno area. A nice respite from over-crowded courses in town!  The staff was extremely friendly and helpful. We felt very welcome.  The practice facilities are awesome! The course was in very good condition.  The tee boxes were level with great grass. The fairways were nice and tight. The greens were a nice speed for a mountain course. The course isn't extremely challenging from the ladies' tees, which makes for an enjoyable round. The home construction did not bother us at all. The views were outstanding and the weather was a perfect 75 degrees.   If you want a pleasant, uncrowded and relaxing golf round, this is your course. I will play this course again!< /Text>

Came for Little League night. Teams from the surrounding areas get to walk the field with their teams and banners. My grandsons like getting autographs from the players. A great place to take in a ballgame.  They put on fun activities between every half inning.  An inexpensive family venue.  Mascot Thunder is terrific and better than many MLB team's mascots.  Great "premium seating"  that doesn't  come at a "premium" price.  Seats behind Home Plate only $13!! Each.  Only 70 miles from San Diego.  Hot dogs, pizza,Baskin Robbins ice cream, all top notch.  A new lounge area down third baseline and a sit-down restaurant add class and ambiance.  Plenty of parking including ADA available only 5 bucks.  Plenty of accessible seating in varying price ranges available< /text>

<user>105818865737305502814<//user>< Text>
Terrible vehicle traffic pattern in and out of stadium.  Seating would have been good had "deck" seats been explained at all on the website.  The "grass" out along the right field foul line is basically a dirt berm.  Not much positive about that area.  When there are a lot of people like the 4th of July all inconvienves are amplified.  Advice for a better experience...go early, buy a regular seat at least a week prior, (do not expect to be comfortable in the grass), expect to pay $5 for parking, $7 for the kid zone experience and expect to spend a lot on concessions, you'll have a much better time knowing these things.< /Text>

<time>1497464193925<//time><Rate>4</Rate><text>This is a minor league baseball park, home to Lake Elsinore Storm, affiliate of the San Diego Padres. Besides the game itself, entertainment always includes enjoyable skits mostly focusing on kids' participation. Venu is laid out well, partially because attendance is fairly sparse, depending on draw of team's opponents. Parking fee is pretty low and located close to the entrance of the park. And, there are special attractions almost every game like fireworks on many Fridays and flat-out free hot dogs on other days. As a senior riding a motorcycle to the games, there are double savings. Tickets for seats just feet away from home plate are an unbelievable$10. Once inside, PA system announces players' names and other information that doesn't interfere with actual play on the field. Personally, I plan to attend as many games as my schedule allows.< /text>< user>
